			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the retail chain. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Walmart_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Walmart (disambiguation)">Walmart (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Walmart Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small> </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>; formerly <b>Wal-Mart Stores, Inc.</b>) is an American multinational retail corporation that operates a chain of hypermarkets, discount department stores, and grocery stores, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville, Arkansas</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>  The company was founded by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> in 1962 and incorporated on October 31, 1969. It also owns and operates <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> retail warehouses.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Location_WorldMap_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Location_WorldMap-10">[10]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart has 11,503 stores and clubs in 27<span class="nowrap"> </span>countries, operating under 56 different<span class="nowrap"> </span>names.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup> The company operates under the name Walmart in the United States and Canada, as <a href="/wiki/Walmart_de_M%C3%A9xico_y_Centroam%C3%A9rica" title="Walmart de México y Centroamérica">Walmart de México y Centroamérica</a> in Mexico and Central America, as <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> in the United Kingdom, as the <a href="/wiki/Seiyu_Group" title="Seiyu Group">Seiyu Group</a> in Japan, and as Best Price in India. It has wholly owned operations in Argentina, Chile, Canada, and South Africa. Since August 2018, Walmart only holds a minority stake in Walmart Brasil, which was renamed Grupo Big in August 2019, with 20 percent of the company's shares, and private equity firm <a href="/wiki/Advent_International" title="Advent International">Advent International</a> holding 80 percent ownership of the company.

//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$14.881 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(FY 2020)</span><sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$236.495 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(FY 2020)</span><sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$74.669 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(FY 2020)</span><sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Owner</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton family</a> (51%)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li>2.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>million, Worldwide (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li>1.5<span class="nowrap"> </span>million, U.S. (2017)<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li>700,000, International</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Division_(business)" title="Division (business)">Divisions</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li>Walmart U.S.</li><li>Walmart International</li><li><a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a></li><li>Global eCommerce</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_Walmart" title="List of assets owned by Walmart">List of subsidiaries</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://walmart.com">walmart<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-Form10K_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Form10K-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OurBusiness_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OurBusiness-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsdaUK_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsdaUK-7">[7]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Walmart is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_companies_by_revenue" title="List of largest companies by revenue">world's largest company by revenue</a>, with <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>514.405 billion, according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Global 500</a> list in 2019. It is also the largest private employer in the world with 2.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>million employees. It is a publicly traded family-owned business, as the company is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Walton_family" title="Walton family">Walton family</a>. Sam Walton's heirs own over 50 percent of Walmart through their holding company Walton Enterprises and through their individual holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Walmart was the largest U.S. grocery retailer in 2019, and 65 percent of Walmart's <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>510.329<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span> sales came from U.S. operations.<sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>Walmart was listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in 1972. By 1988, it was the most profitable retailer in the U.S.,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and it had become the largest in terms of revenue by October 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The company originally was geographically limited to the South and lower Midwest, but it had stores from coast to coast by the early 1990s. Sam's Club opened in New Jersey in November 1989, and the first California outlet opened in <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_California" title="Lancaster, California">Lancaster, California</a>, in July 1990. A Walmart in <a href="/wiki/York,_Pennsylvania" title="York, Pennsylvania">York, Pennsylvania</a> opened in October 1990, the first main store in the Northeast.<sup id="cite_ref-Warner_90_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warner_90-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>Walmart's investments outside the U.S. have seen mixed results. Its operations and subsidiaries in Canada, the United Kingdom, Central America, South America and China are highly successful, whereas its ventures failed in Germany and South Korea.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Walmart" title="History of Walmart">History of Walmart</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1945.E2.80.931969:_Early_history"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1945–1969:_Early_history">1945–1969: Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1945–1969: Early history" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store,_Bentonville,_Arkansas.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="Picture of Sam Walton's original Five and Dime store in Bentonville, Arkansas, now serving as The Walmart Museum." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg/220px-Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg/220px-Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store%2C_Bentonville%2C_Arkansas.jpg" data-alt="Picture of Sam Walton's original Five and Dime store in Bentonville, Arkansas, now serving as The Walmart Museum." data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walton%27s_Five_and_Dime_store,_Bentonville,_Arkansas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sam Walton's original Walton's Five and Dime Store in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville, Arkansas</a>, now serving as The Walmart Museum</div></div></div>
<p>In 1945, businessman and former <a href="/wiki/J._C._Penney" title="J. C. Penney">J. C. Penney</a> employee <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> bought a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Ben_Franklin_(company)" title="Ben Franklin (company)">Ben Franklin</a> stores from the <a href="/wiki/Butler_Brothers" title="Butler Brothers">Butler Brothers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-madeinamerica_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-madeinamerica-17">[17]</a></sup> His primary focus was selling products at low prices to get higher-volume sales at a lower profit margin, portraying it as a crusade for the consumer. He experienced setbacks because the lease price and branch purchase were unusually high, but he was able to find lower-cost suppliers than those used by other stores and was consequently able to undercut his competitors on pricing.<sup id="cite_ref-a_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-18">[18]</a></sup> Sales increased 45 percent in his first year of ownership to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,000</span> in revenue, which increased to $140,000 the next year and $175,000 the year after that. Within the fifth year, the store was generating $250,000 in revenue. The lease then expired for the location and Walton was unable to reach an agreement for renewal, so he opened up a new store at 105 N. Main Street in Bentonville, naming it "Walton's Five and Dime".<sup id="cite_ref-a_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BriefHistory_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BriefHistory-19">[19]</a></sup> That store is now the Walmart Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo1.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Walmartlogo1.png/220px-Walmartlogo1.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="45" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="221" data-file-height="45"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 45px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Walmartlogo1.png/220px-Walmartlogo1.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="45" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Original logo, 1962–1964</div></div></div>
<p>On July 2, 1962, Walton opened the first Walmart Discount City store at 719 W. Walnut Street in <a href="/wiki/Rogers,_Arkansas" title="Rogers, Arkansas">Rogers, Arkansas</a>. The building is now occupied by a hardware store and an antiques mall, while the company's "Store #1" has since expanded to a Supercenter several blocks west at 2110 W. Walnut Street. Within its first five years, the company expanded to 24 stores in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> and reached <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12.6<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span> in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-discountcity_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discountcity-21">[21]</a></sup> In 1968, it opened its first stores outside Arkansas in <a href="/wiki/Sikeston,_Missouri" title="Sikeston, Missouri">Sikeston, Missouri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claremore,_Oklahoma" title="Claremore, Oklahoma">Claremore, Oklahoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1969.E2.80.931990:_Incorporation_and_growth_as_a_regional_power"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1969–1990:_Incorporation_and_growth_as_a_regional_power">1969–1990: Incorporation and growth as a regional power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1969–1990: Incorporation and growth as a regional power" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo2.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Walmartlogo2.png/220px-Walmartlogo2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="53" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="227" data-file-height="55"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 53px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Walmartlogo2.png/220px-Walmartlogo2.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="53" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmartlogo2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used 1964–1981</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg/220px-Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="31" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="71"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 31px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg/220px-Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="31" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg/330px-Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg/440px-Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_1980s_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used 1981–1992</div></div></div>
<p>The company was <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> as <b>Wal-Mart, Inc.</b> on October 31, 1969, and changed its name to <b>Wal-Mart Stores, Inc.</b> in 1970. The same year, the company opened a home office and first distribution center in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. It had 38<span class="nowrap"> </span>stores operating with 1,500 employees and sales of $44.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>million. It began trading stock as a <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">publicly held company</a> on October 1, 1970, and was soon listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Stock_split" title="Stock split">stock split</a> occurred in May 1971 at a price of $47 per share. By this time, Walmart was operating in five states: Arkansas, Kansas, Louisiana, Missouri, and Oklahoma; it entered Tennessee in 1973 and Kentucky and Mississippi in 1974. As the company moved into Texas in 1975, there were 125<span class="nowrap"> </span>stores with 7,500 employees and total sales of $340.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>In the 1980s, Walmart continued to grow rapidly, and by the company's 25th anniversary in 1987, there were 1,198 stores with sales of $15.9<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion and 200,000 associates.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>This year also marked the completion of the company's satellite network, a $24<span class="nowrap"> </span>million investment linking all stores with two-way voice and data transmissions and one-way video communications with the Bentonville office. At the time, the company was the largest private satellite network, allowing the corporate office to track inventory and sales and to instantly communicate to stores.<sup id="cite_ref-satellite_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-satellite-23">[23]</a></sup> By 1984, Sam Walton had begun to source between 6% and 40% of his company's products from China.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1988, Walton stepped down as CEO and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/David_Glass_(businessman)" title="David Glass (businessman)">David Glass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_88_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_88-25">[25]</a></sup> Walton remained as Chairman of the Board.
</p><p>With the contribution of its superstores, the company surpassed <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title='Toys "R" Us'>Toys "R" Us</a> in toy sales in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes_04_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes_04-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1990.E2.80.932005:_Retail_rise_to_multinational_status"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990–2005:_Retail_rise_to_multinational_status">1990–2005: Retail rise to multinational status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1990–2005: Retail rise to multinational status" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_logo,_1992%E2%80%932008.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg/220px-Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="31" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="43"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 31px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg/220px-Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="31" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg/330px-Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg/440px-Wal-Mart_logo%2C_1992%E2%80%932008.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_logo,_1992%E2%80%932008.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used 1992–2008</div></div></div>
<p>While it was the third-largest retailer in the United States, Walmart was more profitable than rivals <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> by the late 1980s. By 1990, it became the largest U.S. retailer by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes_90_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes_90-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>Prior to the summer of 1990, Walmart had no presence on the West Coast or in the Northeast (except for a single Sam's Club in New Jersey which opened in November 1989), but in July and October that year, it opened its first stores in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, respectively. By the mid-1990s, it was far and away the most powerful retailer in the U.S. and expanded into Mexico in 1991 and Canada in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Walmart stores opened throughout the rest of the U.S., with Vermont being the last state to get a store in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-PBS04_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PBS04-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>The company also opened stores outside North America, entering South America in 1995 with stores in Argentina and Brazil; and Europe in July 1999, buying <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> in the United Kingdom for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>In 1997, Walmart was <a href="/wiki/Historical_components_of_the_Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Historical components of the Dow Jones Industrial Average">added</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>In 1998, Walmart introduced the Neighborhood Market concept with three stores in Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-grocerybiz_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grocerybiz-33">[33]</a></sup> By 2005, estimates indicate that the company controlled about 20 percent of the retail grocery and consumables business.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Scott_(businessman)" title="Lee Scott (businessman)">H. Lee Scott</a> became Walmart's President and CEO as the company's sales increased to $165<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2000sales_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000sales-35">[35]</a></sup> In 2002, it was listed for the first time as America's largest corporation on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list, with revenues of $219.8<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion and profits of $6.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion. It has remained there every year except 2006, 2009, and 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-2007-Fortune-500_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007-Fortune-500-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2006-Fortune-500_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2006-Fortune-500-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, Walmart reported <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$312.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span> in sales, more than 6,200 facilities around the world—including 3,800 stores in the United States and 2,800 elsewhere, employing more than 1.6<span class="nowrap"> </span>million associates. Its U.S. presence grew so rapidly that only small pockets of the country remained more than 60 miles (97 kilometers) from the nearest store.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>As Walmart rapidly expanded into the world's largest corporation, many critics worried about its effect on local communities, particularly small towns with many "<a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">mom and pop</a>" stores. There have been several studies on the economic impact of Walmart on small towns and local businesses, jobs, and taxpayers. In one, Kenneth Stone, a professor of economics at <a href="/wiki/Iowa_State_University" title="Iowa State University">Iowa State University</a>, found that some small towns can lose almost half of their retail trade within ten years of a Walmart store opening.<sup id="cite_ref-Rural_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rural-48">[48]</a></sup> However, in another study, he compared the changes to what small town shops had faced in the past—including the development of the railroads, the advent of the Sears Roebuck catalog, and the arrival of shopping malls—and concluded that shop owners who adapt to changes in the retail market can thrive after Walmart arrives.<sup id="cite_ref-Rural_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rural-48">[48]</a></sup> A later study in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_State_University" title="Mississippi State University">Mississippi State University</a> showed that there are "both positive and negative impacts on existing stores in the area where the new supercenter locates."<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_Artz_Myles_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone_Artz_Myles-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in September 2005, Walmart used its logistics network to organize a rapid response to the disaster, donating $20<span class="nowrap"> </span>million, 1,500 truckloads of merchandise, food for 100,000 meals, and the promise of a job for every one of its displaced workers.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> An independent study by Steven Horwitz of <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_University" title="St. Lawrence University">St. Lawrence University</a> found that Walmart, <a href="/wiki/The_Home_Depot" title="The Home Depot">The Home Depot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">Lowe's</a> made use of their local knowledge about supply chains, infrastructure, decision makers and other resources to provide emergency supplies and reopen stores well before the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA) began its response.<sup id="cite_ref-Kouzes_10_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kouzes_10-51">[51]</a></sup> While the company was overall lauded for its quick response amidst <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of government response to Hurricane Katrina">criticism</a> of FEMA, several critics were quick to point out that there still remained issues with the company's labor relations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2005.E2.80.932010:_Initiatives"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005–2010:_Initiatives">2005–2010: Initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2005–2010: Initiatives" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_on_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="Arial view of dozens of solar panels distributed around the roof of a Walmart store" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg/220px-Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2198" data-file-height="1318"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 132px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg/220px-Solar_Panels_on_Caguas%2C_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" data-alt="Arial view of dozens of solar panels distributed around the roof of a Walmart store" data-width="220" data-height="132" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Panels_on_Caguas,_Puerto_Rico_Walmart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solar modules mounted on a Walmart Supercenter in <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas, Puerto Rico</a></div></div></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_initiatives">Environmental initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Environmental initiatives" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In November 2005, Walmart announced several environmental measures to increase <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a> and improve its overall environmental record, which had previously been lacking.<sup id="cite_ref-GuntherMark_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuntherMark-53">[53]</a></sup> The company's primary goals included spending $500 million a year to increase fuel efficiency in Walmart's truck fleet by 25 percent over three years and double it within ten; reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions by 20 percent in seven years; reduce energy use at stores by 30 percent; and cut solid waste from U.S. stores and Sam's Clubs by 25 percent in three years. CEO Lee Scott said that Walmart's goal was to be a "good steward of the environment" and ultimately use only <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> sources and produce <a href="/wiki/Zero_waste" title="Zero waste">zero waste</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-going_green_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-going_green-54">[54]</a></sup> The company also designed three new experimental stores with <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> solar panels, <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>-capable boilers, water-cooled refrigerators, and <a href="/wiki/Xeriscaping" title="Xeriscaping">xeriscape</a> gardens.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In this time, Walmart also became the biggest seller of organic milk and the biggest buyer of organic cotton in the world, while reducing packaging and energy costs.<sup id="cite_ref-GuntherMark_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuntherMark-53">[53]</a></sup> In 2007, the company worked with outside consultants to discover its total environmental impact and find areas for improvement. Walmart created its own <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_industry" title="Electric power industry">electric company</a> in Texas, Texas Retail Energy, planned to supply its stores with cheap power purchased at wholesale prices. Through this new venture, the company expected to save $15 million annually and also to lay the groundwork and infrastructure to sell electricity to Texas consumers in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-redorbit_electricity_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redorbit_electricity-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding_and_store_design_changes">Branding and store design changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Branding and store design changes" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2006, Walmart announced that it would remodel its U.S. stores to help it appeal to a wider variety of demographics, including more affluent shoppers. As part of the initiative, the company launched a new store in Plano, Texas, that included high-end electronics, jewelry, expensive wines and a sushi bar.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p><p>On September 12, 2007, Walmart introduced new advertising with the <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogan</a>, "<i>Save money. Live better.</i>", replacing "<i>Always Low Prices, Always</i>", which it had used for the previous 19 years. <a href="/wiki/Global_Insight" title="Global Insight">Global Insight</a>, which conducted the research that supported the ads, found that Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Price_level" title="Price level">price level</a> reduction resulted in savings for consumers of $287 billion in 2006, which equated to $957 per person or $2,500 per household (up 7.3 percent from the 2004 savings estimate of $2,329).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>On June 30, 2008, Walmart removed the hyphen from its logo and replaced the star with a <i>Spark</i> symbol that resembles a sunburst, flower, or star. The new logo received mixed reviews from design critics who questioned whether the new logo was as bold as those of competitors, such as the <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> bullseye, or as instantly recognizable as the previous company logo, which was used for 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The new logo made its debut on the company's website on July 1, 2008, and its U.S. locations updated store logos in the fall of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-new_logo_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_logo-60">[60]</a></sup> Walmart Canada started to adopt the logo for its stores in early 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions_and_employee_benefits">Acquisitions and employee benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Acquisitions and employee benefits" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On March 20, 2009, Walmart announced that it was paying a combined <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$933.6<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span> in bonuses to every full and part-time hourly worker.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> This was in addition to $788.8 million in <a href="/wiki/Profit_sharing" title="Profit sharing">profit sharing</a>, <a href="/wiki/401(k)" title="401(k)">401(k)</a> pension contributions, hundreds of millions of dollars in merchandise discounts, and contributions to the employees' stock purchase plan.<sup id="cite_ref-Maestri_09_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maestri_09-63">[63]</a></sup> While the economy at large was in an ongoing <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a>, Walmart reported solid financial figures for the most recent fiscal year (ending January 31, 2009), with $401.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion in net sales, a gain of 7.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent from the prior year. Income from continuing operations increased 3<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent to $13.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion, and earnings per share rose 6<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent to $3.35.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>On February 22, 2010, the company confirmed it was acquiring <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">video streaming</a> company <a href="/wiki/Vudu,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Vudu, Inc.">Vudu, Inc.</a> for an estimated $100<span class="nowrap"> </span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Continued_developments"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–present:_Continued_developments">2011–present: Continued developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2011–present: Continued developments" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg/300px-Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="78" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2464" data-file-height="642"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 300px;height: 78px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg/300px-Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="300" data-height="78" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart%E2%80%99s_Grease_Fuel_Truck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A truck converted to run on biofuel</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg/220px-WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg/220px-WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalmartPickupRichmondHill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Walmart Pickup location in Canada</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart's truck fleet logs millions of miles each year, and the company planned to double the fleet's efficiency between 2005 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The truck pictured is one of 15 based at Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Buckeye,_Arizona" title="Buckeye, Arizona">Buckeye, Arizona</a>, distribution center that was converted to run on <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> from reclaimed cooking grease made during food preparation at Walmart stores.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2011, Walmart announced a program to improve the nutritional value of its store brands over five years, gradually reducing the amount of salt and sugar and completely eliminating <a href="/wiki/Trans_fat" title="Trans fat">trans fat</a>. Walmart also promised to negotiate with suppliers with respect to nutritional issues, reduce prices for whole foods and vegetables, and open stores in low-income areas, so-called "<a href="/wiki/Food_desert" title="Food desert">food deserts</a>", where there are no supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On April 23, 2011, the company announced that it was testing its new "Walmart To Go" home delivery system where customers will be able to order specific items offered on their website. The initial test was in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, and the company has not yet said whether the delivery system will be rolled out nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_11_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_11-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>On November 14, 2012, Walmart launched its first mail subscription service called Goodies. Customers pay a $7 monthly subscription for five to eight delivered food samples each month, so they can try new foods.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The service shut down in late 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2013, the firm announced it was in talks to acquire a majority stake in the <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>-based supermarket chain, <a href="/wiki/Naivas" class="mw-redirect" title="Naivas">Naivas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2014, some Walmart employees went on strike in major U.S. cities demanding higher wages.<sup id="cite_ref-CNNMoney_Walmart_2014-06-04_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney_Walmart_2014-06-04-73">[73]</a></sup> In July 2014, American actor and comedian <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan" title="Tracy Morgan">Tracy Morgan</a> launched a lawsuit against Walmart seeking punitive damages over a multi-car pile-up which the suit alleges was caused by the driver of one of the firm's tractor-trailers who had not slept for 24 hours. Morgan's limousine was apparently hit by the trailer, injuring him and two fellow passengers and killing a fourth, fellow comedian James McNair.<sup id="cite_ref-MorganWalmart_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MorganWalmart-74">[74]</a></sup> Walmart settled with the McNair family for $10 million, while admitting no liability.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Morgan and Walmart reached a settlement in 2015 for an undisclosed amount,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> though Walmart later accused its insurers of "bad faith" in refusing to pay the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, the company closed five stores on short notice for plumbing repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> However, employees and the <a href="/wiki/United_Food_and_Commercial_Workers_International_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="United Food and Commercial Workers International Union">United Food and Commercial Workers International Union</a> (UFCW) alleged some stores were closed in retaliation for strikes aimed at increasing wages and improving working conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The UFCW filed a complaint with the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board" title="National Labor Relations Board">National Labor Relations Board</a>. All five stores have since reopened.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, Walmart was the biggest US commercial producer of <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> with 142 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">capacity</a>, and had 17 <a href="/wiki/Energy_storage" title="Energy storage">energy storage</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> This solar was primarily on rooftops, whereas there is an additional 20,000 m<sup>2</sup> for solar canopies over parking lots.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>On January 15, 2016, Walmart announced it would close 269 stores in 2016, affecting 16,000 workers.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> One hundred and fifty-four of these stores earmarked for closure were in the U.S. (150 Walmart U.S. stores, 115 Walmart International stores, and 4<span class="nowrap"> </span>Sam's Clubs). Ninety-five percent of these U.S. stores were located, on average, 10 miles from another Walmart store.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup> The 269 stores represented less than 1<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent of global square footage and revenue for the company. All 102 locations of Walmart Express, which had been in a pilot program since 2011, were included in the closures. Walmart planned to focus on "strengthening Supercenters, optimizing Neighborhood Markets, growing the e-commerce business and expanding pickup services for customers". In fiscal 2017, the company plans to open between 50 and 60 Supercenters, 85 to 95 Neighborhood Markets, 7 to 10 Sam's Clubs, and 200 to 240 international locations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup> At the end of fiscal 2017, Walmart opened 38 Supercenters and relocated, expanded or converted 21 discount stores into Supercenters, for a total of 59 Supercenters, and opened 69 Neighborhood Markets, 8 Sam's Clubs, and 173 international locations, and relocated, expanded or converted 4 locations for a total of 177 international locations. On August 8, 2016, Walmart announced a deal to acquire e-commerce website Jet.com for US$3.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Jet.com co-founder and <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Lore" title="Marc Lore">Marc Lore</a> stayed on to run Jet.com in addition to Walmart's existing U.S. e-commerce operation. The acquisition was structured as a payout of $3 billion in cash, and an additional $300 million in Walmart stock vested over time as part of an incentive bonus plan for Jet.com executives.<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart-Inc-Aug-2016-8-K_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart-Inc-Aug-2016-8-K-88">[88]</a></sup> On October 19, 2016, Walmart announced it would partner with IBM and Tsinghua University to track the pork supply chain in China using blockchain.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>On February 15, 2017, Walmart announced the acquisition of Moosejaw, a leading online active outdoor retailer, for approximately $51 million. The acquisition closed on February 13, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On June 16, 2017, Walmart agreed to acquire the men's apparel company <a href="/wiki/Bonobos_(apparel)" title="Bonobos (apparel)">Bonobos</a> for $310 million in an effort to expand its fashion holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On September 29, 2017, Walmart acquired Parcel, a technology-based, same-day and last-mile delivery company in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The acquisition announcement saw Walmart shares rise more than 1%.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On December 6, 2017, Walmart announced that it will change its corporate name to Walmart Inc. from Wal-Mart Stores, Inc. effective February 1, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart-Inc-Dec-2017-8-K_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart-Inc-Dec-2017-8-K-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walmart_Inc_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart_Inc-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>On January 11, 2018, Walmart announced that 63 Sam's Club locations in cities including <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, and others would be closing. Some of the stores had already liquidated, without notifying employees; some employees learned by a company-wide email delivered January 11. All of the 63 stores were gone from the Sam's Club website as of the morning of January 11. Walmart said that ten of the stores will become e-commerce distribution centers and employees can reapply to work at those locations. <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> magazine calculated that over 11,000 workers will be affected.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> On the same day, Walmart announced that as a result of <a href="/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017" title="Tax Cuts and Jobs Act of 2017">the new tax law</a>, it would be raising Walmart starting wages, distributing bonuses, expanding its leave policies and contributing toward the cost of employees' adoptions. <a href="/wiki/Doug_McMillon" title="Doug McMillon">Doug McMillon</a>, Walmart's CEO, said, "We are early in the stages of assessing the opportunities tax reform creates for us to invest in our customers and associates and to further strengthen our business, all of which should benefit our shareholders."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2018, Walmart announced that it is producing its own brand of <a href="/wiki/Meal_kits" class="mw-redirect" title="Meal kits">meal kits</a> in all of its stores that is priced under <a href="/wiki/Blue_Apron" title="Blue Apron">Blue Apron</a> designed to serve two people.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p><p>It was reported that Walmart is now looking at entering the subscription-video space, hoping to compete with Netflix and Amazon. They have enlisted the help of former <a href="/wiki/Epix" title="Epix">Epix</a> CEO, Mark Greenberg, to help develop a low-cost subscription video-streaming service.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2018, Walmart partnered with comedian and talk show host <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> to launch a new brand of women's apparel and accessories called EV1.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>On February 26, 2019, Walmart announced that it had acquired Tel Aviv-based product review start-up Aspectiva for an undisclosed sum.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2019, Walmart announced the launch of free one-day shipping on more than 220,000 items with minimum purchase amount of $35.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The initiative first launched in Las Vegas and the Phoenix area.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2019, Walmart made the announcement that it would cease the sale of all e-cigarettes due to "regulatory complexity and uncertainty" over the products. Earlier in 2019, Walmart stopped selling fruit-flavored e-cigarette and had raised the minimum age to 21 for the purchase of products containing tobacco.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> That same month, Walmart opened its first Health Center, a "medical mall" where customers can purchase primary care services, such as: vision tests, dental exams and root canals, lab work, X-rays and EKGs, counseling, and fitness and diet classes. Prices without insurance were listed, for instance, at $30 for an annual physical and $45 for a counseling session.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>As of October 2019, Walmart stopped selling all live fish and aquatic plants.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg/220px-Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2209" data-file-height="2267"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 226px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg/220px-Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="226" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Coronavirus_notices.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Signs on a Walmart indicated changes due to the Coronavirus</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2020, due to the <a href="/wiki/2019-20_coronavirus_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="2019-20 coronavirus pandemic">2019-20 coronavirus pandemic</a> outbreak, Walmart changed some of its employee benefits. Employees can now decide to stay home and take unpaid leave if they feel unable to work or uncomfortable coming to work. Additionally, Walmart employees who contract the virus will receive "up to two weeks of pay". After two weeks, hourly associates who aren't able to return to work are eligible for up to 26 weeks in pay.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_divisions">Operating divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Operating divisions" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMart_international_locations.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/220px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 113px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/220px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="113" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/330px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/WalMart_international_locations.svg/440px-WalMart_international_locations.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WalMart_international_locations.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Walmart international locations (former locations in red)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_Walmart" title="List of assets owned by Walmart">List of assets owned by Walmart</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_footprint.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walmart_footprint.png/220px-Walmart_footprint.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1859" data-file-height="968"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 115px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walmart_footprint.png/220px-Walmart_footprint.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="115" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_footprint.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Walmart stores in the U.S., as of August 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Walmart's operations are organized into four divisions: Walmart U.S., Walmart International, <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> and Global eCommerce.<sup id="cite_ref-annrep_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annrep-109">[109]</a></sup> The company offers various retail formats throughout these divisions, including supercenters, supermarkets, hypermarkets, warehouse clubs, cash-and-carry stores, home improvement, specialty electronics, restaurants, apparel stores, drugstores, convenience stores, and digital retail.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_19-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_U.S.">Walmart U.S.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Walmart U.S." data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><b>Walmart U.S.</b> is the company's largest division, accounting for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$331.666<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span>, or 65 percent of total sales, for fiscal 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-13">[13]</a></sup> It consists of three retail formats that have become commonplace in the United States: <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">Supercenters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discount_store" title="Discount store">Discount Stores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">Neighborhood Markets</a>, and other small formats. The discount stores sell a variety of mostly non-grocery products, though emphasis has now shifted towards supercenters, which include more groceries. As of January 31, 2019,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are a total of 4,756 Walmart U.S. stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> In the United States, 90 percent of the population resides within 10 miles of a Walmart store.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The total number of Walmart U.S. and Sam's Club combined is 5,355.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p><p>The president and CEO of Walmart U.S. is John Furner.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Supercenter">Walmart Supercenter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Walmart Supercenter" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Supercenter,_North_Windham,_CT.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="A Walmart Supercenter store" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Walmart_Supercenter%2C_North_Windham%2C_CT.jpg/220px-Walmart_Supercenter%2C_North_Windham%2C_CT.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Walmart_Supercenter%2C_North_Windham%2C_CT.jpg/220px-Walmart_Supercenter%2C_North_Windham%2C_CT.jpg" data-alt="A Walmart Supercenter store" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Supercenter,_North_Windham,_CT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Walmart Supercenter in <a href="/wiki/Windham,_Connecticut" title="Windham, Connecticut">Windham, Connecticut</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Walmart Supercenters</b>, branded simply as "Walmart", are <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">hypermarkets</a> with sizes varying from 69,000 to 260,000 square feet (6,400 to 24,200 square meters), but averaging about 178,000 square feet (16,500 square meters).<sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup> These stock general merchandise and a full-service supermarket, including meat and poultry, <a href="/wiki/Baking" title="Baking">baked goods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delicatessen" title="Delicatessen">delicatessen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frozen_food" title="Frozen food">frozen foods</a>, dairy products, garden <a href="/wiki/Produce" title="Produce">produce</a>, and fresh seafood. Many Walmart Supercenters also have a garden center, <a href="/wiki/Pet_store" title="Pet store">pet shop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a>, Tire &amp; <a href="/wiki/Oil_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil change">Lube</a> Express, optical center, <a href="/wiki/Photographic_processing" title="Photographic processing">one-hour photo processing lab</a>, portrait studio, and numerous alcove shops, such as cellular phone stores, hair and nail salons, video rental stores, local bank branches (such as <a href="/wiki/Woodforest_National_Bank" title="Woodforest National Bank">Woodforest National Bank</a> branches in newer locations), and fast food outlets.
</p><p>Many Walmart Supercenters have featured <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> restaurants, but in 2007, Walmart announced it would stop opening McDonald's restaurants at most of their newer stores, most likely due to nutritional concerns. Most locations that opened up after the announcement had Subway as their restaurants, and some McDonald's inside the stores were replaced with <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In some Canadian locations, Tim Hortons were opened. Recently, in several Supercenters, like the <a href="/wiki/Tallahassee,_Florida" title="Tallahassee, Florida">Tallahassee, Florida</a>, location, Walmart added <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> to their locations, and the location in <a href="/wiki/Glen_Burnie,_Maryland" title="Glen Burnie, Maryland">Glen Burnie, Maryland</a>, due to its past as a hypermarket called Leedmark, which operated from  May 1991 to January 1994, boasts an <a href="/wiki/Auntie_Anne%27s" title="Auntie Anne's">Auntie Anne's</a> and an Italian restaurant.
</p><p>Some locations also have fuel stations which sell gasoline distributed by <a href="/wiki/Murphy_USA" title="Murphy USA">Murphy USA</a> (which spun off from <a href="/wiki/Murphy_Oil" title="Murphy Oil">Murphy Oil</a> in 2013), <a href="/wiki/Sunoco,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Sunoco, Inc.">Sunoco, Inc.</a> ("Optima"), the <a href="/wiki/Tesoro" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesoro">Tesoro</a> Corporation ("Mirastar"), USA Gasoline, and even now Walmart-branded gas stations.<sup id="cite_ref-CSNews_WMGas_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSNews_WMGas-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>The first Supercenter opened in Washington, Missouri, in 1988. A similar concept, <a href="/wiki/Hypermart_USA" title="Hypermart USA">Hypermart USA</a>, had opened a year earlier in <a href="/wiki/Garland,_Texas" title="Garland, Texas">Garland, Texas</a>. All Hypermart USA stores were later closed or converted into Supercenters.
</p><p>As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were 3,571 Walmart Supercenters in 49 of the 50 U.S. states, the District of Columbia, and Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Hawaii is the only state to not have a Supercenter location. The largest Supercenter in the world, covering 260,000 square feet (24,000 square meters) on two floors, is located in <a href="/wiki/Crossgates_Commons" title="Crossgates Commons">Crossgates Commons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>A typical supercenter sells approximately 120,000 items, compared to the 35 million products sold in Walmart's online store.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>The "Supercenter" name has since been phased out, with these stores now simply referred to as "Walmart", since the company introduced the new Walmart logo in 2008. However, the branding is still used in Walmart's Canadian stores (spelled as "Supercentre" in Canadian English).<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Discount_Store">Walmart Discount Store</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Walmart Discount Store" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte,_NC_(7580001150).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="The exterior of the Walmart Discount Store in Charlotte, North Carolina" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg/220px-Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg/220px-Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte%2C_NC_%287580001150%29.jpg" data-alt="The exterior of the Walmart Discount Store in Charlotte, North Carolina" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wal-Mart_Albemarle_Rd_Charlotte,_NC_(7580001150).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of the Walmart Discount Store in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Walmart Discount Stores</b>, also branded as simply "Walmart", are discount department stores with sizes varying from 30,000 to 206,000 square feet (2,800 to 19,100 square meters), with the average store covering 105,000 square feet (9,800 square meters).<sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup> They carry <a href="/wiki/General_merchandise" class="mw-redirect" title="General merchandise">general merchandise</a> and limited <a href="/wiki/Grocery" class="mw-redirect" title="Grocery">groceries</a>. Some newer and remodeled discount stores have an expanded grocery department, similar to Target's PFresh department. Many of these stores also feature a garden center, pharmacy, Tire &amp; Lube Express, optical center, one-hour photo processing lab, portrait studio, a bank branch, a cell phone store, and a fast food outlet. Some also have gasoline stations.<sup id="cite_ref-CSNews_WMGas_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSNews_WMGas-114">[114]</a></sup> Discount Stores were Walmart's original concept, though they have since been surpassed by Supercenters.
</p><p>In 1990, Walmart opened its first Bud's Discount City location in Bentonville. Bud's operated as a closeout store, much like <a href="/wiki/Big_Lots" title="Big Lots">Big Lots</a>. Many locations were opened to fulfill leases in shopping centers as Walmart stores left and moved into newly built Supercenters. All of the Bud's Discount City stores had closed or converted into Walmart Discount Stores by 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-DSN_Retailing_Today_97_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSN_Retailing_Today_97-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>At its peak in 1996, there were 1,995 Walmart Discount Stores,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> but as of January 31, 2020, that number was dropped to 376.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_Neighborhood_Market">Walmart Neighborhood Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Walmart Neighborhood Market" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_GA125,_Valdosta.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_GA125%2C_Valdosta.jpg/220px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_GA125%2C_Valdosta.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_GA125%2C_Valdosta.jpg/220px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_GA125%2C_Valdosta.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_GA125,_Valdosta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Walmart Neighborhood Market in <a href="/wiki/Valdosta,_Georgia" title="Valdosta, Georgia">Valdosta, Georgia</a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Walmart Neighborhood Market</b>, sometimes branded as "Neighborhood Market by Walmart" or informally known as "Neighborhood Walmart", is Walmart's chain of smaller <a href="/wiki/Grocery_stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Grocery stores">grocery stores</a> ranging from 28,000 to 65,000 square feet (2,600 to 6,000 square meters) and averaging about 42,000 square feet (3,900 square metres), about a fifth of the size of a Walmart Supercenter.<sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_October_15_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_October_15-120">[120]</a></sup> The first Walmart Neighborhood Market opened ten years after the first Supercenter opened, yet Walmart renewed its focus on the smaller grocery store format in the 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-Loeb_14_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loeb_14-121">[121]</a></sup></p><p>The stores focus on three of Walmart's major sales categories: groceries, which account for about 55 percent of the company's revenue,<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_13_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_13-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> pharmacy, and, at some stores, fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_July_15_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_July_15-124">[124]</a></sup> For groceries and consumables, the stores sell fresh produce, deli and bakery items, prepared foods, meat, dairy, organic, general grocery and frozen foods, in addition to cleaning products and pet supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_October_15_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_October_15-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mossman_12_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mossman_12-125">[125]</a></sup> Some stores offer wine and beer sales<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_October_15_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_October_15-120">[120]</a></sup> and drive-through pharmacies.<sup id="cite_ref-Gute_15_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gute_15-126">[126]</a></sup> Some stores, such as one at Midtown Center in Bentonville, Arkansas, offer made-to-order pizza with a seating area for eating.<sup id="cite_ref-Gute_15_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gute_15-126">[126]</a></sup> Customers can also use Walmart's site-to-store operation and pick up online orders at Walmart Neighborhood Market stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Stark_12_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark_12-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>Products at Walmart Neighborhood Market stores carry the same prices as those at Walmart's larger supercenters. A <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investor_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Moody's Investor Services">Moody's</a> analyst said the wider company's pricing structure gives the chain of grocery stores a "competitive advantage" over competitors <a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods" class="mw-redirect" title="Whole Foods">Whole Foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trader_Joe%27s" title="Trader Joe's">Trader Joe's</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Peterson_July_15_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peterson_July_15-124">[124]</a></sup> Walmart contributed around 14.5% of the entire quantity of food purchased in the USA during 2016.
