This figure was more than double the contribution from their closest competitor Kroger.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p>Neighborhood Market stores expanded slowly at first as a way to fill gaps between Walmart Supercenters and Discount Stores in existing markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Birchall_10_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birchall_10-129">[129]</a></sup> In its first 12 years, the company opened about 180 Walmart Neighborhood Markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Birchall_10_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birchall_10-129">[129]</a></sup> By 2010, Walmart said it was ready to accelerate its expansion plans for the grocery stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Birchall_10_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birchall_10-129">[129]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were 687 Walmart Neighborhood Markets,<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> each employing between 90 and 95 full-time and part-time workers.<sup id="cite_ref-Darrow_15_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darrow_15-130">[130]</a></sup> There are also currently 12 Amigo supermarkets in Puerto Rico. The total number of Neighborhood Markets and Amigo combined is 699, while the total number of the former two and other small formats combined is 809.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_stores_and_concepts">Former stores and concepts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Former stores and concepts" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_Alma.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG/220px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG/220px-Walmart_Neighborhood_Market%2C_Alma.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Neighborhood_Market,_Alma.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Walmart Express branded as a Walmart Neighborhood Market in <a href="/wiki/Alma,_Georgia" title="Alma, Georgia">Alma, Georgia</a> in September 2015. This location closed in 2016 as part of a plan to close 269 stores globally.</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart opened <b>Supermercado de Walmart</b> locations to appeal to <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> communities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The first one, a 39,000-square-foot (3,600-square-meter) store in the <a href="/wiki/Spring_Branch,_Houston" title="Spring Branch, Houston">Spring Branch</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, opened on April 29, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-HoustonChron_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoustonChron-132">[132]</a></sup> The store was a conversion of an existing Walmart Neighborhood Market.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2009, another Supermercado de Walmart opened in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Both locations closed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In 2009, Walmart opened "Mas Club", a warehouse retail operation patterned after Sam's Club. Its lone store closed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-HoustonChron_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoustonChron-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p><b>Walmart Express</b> was a chain of smaller discount stores with a range of services from groceries to check cashing and gasoline service. The concept was focused on small towns deemed unable to support a larger store, and large cities where space was at a premium. Walmart planned to build 15 to 20 Walmart Express stores, focusing on Arkansas, North Carolina and Chicago, by the end of its fiscal year in January 2012. As of September 2014,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart re-branded all of its Express format stores to Neighborhood Markets in an effort to streamline its retail offer. It continued to open new Express stores under the Neighborhood Market name. As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were 111 small-format stores in the United States. These include E-Commerce Acquisition / C-stores (88 locations, including 80 E-Commerce Acquisition stores and 8 convenience stores) and other store formats (22 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> On January 15, 2016, Walmart announced that it would be closing 269 stores globally, including all 102 U.S. Walmart Express stores, including those branded as Neighborhood Markets.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Initiatives">Initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Initiatives" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In September 2006, Walmart announced a pilot program to sell <a href="/wiki/Generic_drug" title="Generic drug">generic drugs</a> at $4<span class="nowrap"> </span>per prescription. The program was launched at stores in the <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>, area, and by January 2007 had been expanded to all stores in Florida. While the average price of generics is<span class="nowrap"> </span>$29 per prescription, compared to<span class="nowrap"> </span>$102 for name-brand drugs, Walmart maintains that it is not selling at a loss, or providing them as an act of charity—instead, they are using the same mechanisms of mass distribution that it uses to bring lower prices to other products.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Many of Walmart's low cost generics are imported from India, where they are made by drug makers that include <a href="/wiki/Ranbaxy_Laboratories" title="Ranbaxy Laboratories">Ranbaxy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cipla" title="Cipla">Cipla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>On February 6, 2007, the company launched a "beta" version of a movie download service, which sold about 3,000 films and television episodes from all major studios and television networks.<sup id="cite_ref-moviedownload_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moviedownload-139">[139]</a></sup> The service was discontinued on December 21, 2007, due to low sales.<sup id="cite_ref-moviedownloaddiscontinued_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moviedownloaddiscontinued-140">[140]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, Walmart started a pilot program in the small grocery store concept called Marketside in the metropolitan Phoenix, Arizona, area. The four stores closed in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarman_Max_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarman_Max-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, Walmart began testing a free grocery pickup service, allowing customers to select products online and choose their pickup time. At the store, a Walmart employee loads the groceries into the customer's car. As of December 17, 2017,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the service is available in 39 U.S. states.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2016, Walmart announced a change to ShippingPass, its three-day shipping service, and that it will move from a three-day delivery to two-day delivery to remain competitive with Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Walmart priced it at 49 dollars per year, compared to Amazon Prime's 99-dollar-per-year price.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2016, Walmart and Sam's Club announced that they would begin testing a last-mile grocery delivery that used services including <a href="/wiki/Uber" title="Uber">Uber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deliv" title="Deliv">Deliv</a>, to bring customers' orders to their homes. Walmart customers would be able to shop using the company's online grocery service at grocery.walmart.com, then request delivery at checkout for a small fee. The first tests were planned to go live in Denver and Phoenix.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Walmart announced on March 14, 2018, that it would expand online delivery to 100 metropolitan regions in the United States, the equivalent of 40 percent of households, by the end of the year of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p><p>Walmart's Winemakers Selection <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a> wine was introduced in June 2018 in about 1,100 stores. The wine, from domestic and international sources, was described by <i>Washington Post</i> food and wine columnist Dave McIntyre as notably good for the inexpensive ($11 to $16 per bottle) price level.<sup id="cite_ref-wp92818_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp92818-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2019, Walmart announced that customers in 2,000 locations in 29 states can use the grocery pickup service for their adult beverage purchases. Walmart will also deliver adult beverages from nearly 200 stores across California and Florida. <sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2020, Walmart announced a new membership program called, "Walmart +". The news came shortly after Walmart cut ties with its personal shopping service, Jetblack. <sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Walmart_International">Walmart International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Walmart International" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart's international operations comprised 6,148 stores<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and 800,000 workers in 26<span class="nowrap"> </span>countries outside the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart_international_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart_international-152">[152]</a></sup> There are wholly owned operations in Argentina, Brazil, Canada, and the UK. With 2.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>million employees worldwide, the company is the largest private employer in the U.S. and Mexico, and one of the largest in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-OurBusiness_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OurBusiness-6">[6]</a></sup> In fiscal 2019 Walmart's international division sales were <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$120.824<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span>, or 23.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent of total sales.<sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Annual_Report_Page_20-13">[13]</a></sup> International retail units range from 1,400 to 186,000 square feet (130 to 17,280 square metres), while wholesale units range from 25,000 to 156,000 square feet (2,300 to 14,500 square metres).<sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup> Judith McKenna is the president and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart.com_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart.com-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Argentina" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg/220px-Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1348"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 148px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg/220px-Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="148" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Supercenter_Argentina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Walmart Supercenter in Argentina in February 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart Argentina was founded in 1995 and, as of October 31, 2019,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> operates 92 stores under the banners Walmart Supercenter (29 locations), Changomas (53 locations), Mi Changomas (8 locations), and Punto Mayorista (2 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_America">Central America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Central America" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Walmart also owns 51<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent of the Central American Retail Holding Company (CARHCO), which, as of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> consists of 838 stores, including 257 stores in Guatemala (under the Paiz [26 locations], Walmart Supercenter [10 locations], Despensa Familiar [176 locations], and Maxi Dispensa [45 locations] banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 100 stores in El Salvador (under the Despensa Familiar [63 locations], La Despensa de Don Juan [17 locations], Walmart Supercenter [5 locations], and Maxi Despensa [15 locations] banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 110 stores in Honduras (including the Paiz [8 locations], Walmart Supercenter [3 locations], Dispensa Familiar [71 locations], and Maxi Despensa [28 locations] banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 103 stores in Nicaragua (including the Pali [72 locations], La Unión [9 locations], Maxi Pali [20 locations], and Walmart Supercenter [2<span class="nowrap"> </span>locations] banners),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and 268 stores in Costa Rica (including the Maxi Pali [47 locations], Mas X Menos [39 locations], Walmart Supercenter [13<span class="nowrap"> </span>locations], and Pali [169 locations] banners<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-sec2006_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec2006-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chile" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In January 2009, the company acquired a controlling interest in the largest grocer in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, Distribución y Servicio D&amp;S SA.<sup id="cite_ref-Stanford_13_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanford_13-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bustillo_08_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bustillo_08-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2010, the company was renamed <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Walmart Chile">Walmart Chile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Diario_Financiero_10_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diario_Financiero_10-157">[157]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart Chile operates 367 stores under the banners Lider Hiper (87 locations), Lider Express (103 locations), Superbodega Acuenta (116 locations), Ekono (56 locations), and Central Mayorista (5 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Mexico" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Walmart_de_M%C3%A9xico_y_Centroam%C3%A9rica" title="Walmart de México y Centroamérica">Walmart de México y Centroamérica</a></div>
<p>As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart's Mexico division, the largest outside the U.S., consisted of 2,571 stores.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Walmart in Mexico operates Walmart Supercenter (280 locations), Sam's Club (163 locations), Bodega Aurrera (541 locations), Mi Bodega Aurrera (395 locations), Bodega Aurrera Express (1,099 locations), and Superama (93 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Canada" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Canada" title="Walmart Canada">Walmart Canada</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RichmondHillWalmart.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/RichmondHillWalmart.jpg/220px-RichmondHillWalmart.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/RichmondHillWalmart.jpg/220px-RichmondHillWalmart.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RichmondHillWalmart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Walmart Supercentre in <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_Ontario" title="Richmond Hill, Ontario">Richmond Hill, Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> in September 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart has operated in Canada since it acquired 122<span class="nowrap"> </span>stores comprising the <a href="/wiki/Woolco" title="Woolco">Woolco</a> division of <a href="/wiki/F._W._Woolworth_Company" title="F. W. Woolworth Company">Woolworth Canada, Inc</a> on January 14, 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> it operates 408<span class="nowrap"> </span>locations (including 343<span class="nowrap"> </span>supercentres and 65 discount stores)<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and, as of June 2015,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> it employs 89,358 people, with a local home office in <a href="/wiki/Mississauga" title="Mississauga">Mississauga</a>, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-WalmartCanada_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalmartCanada-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Canada" title="Walmart Canada">Walmart Canada</a>'s first three Supercentres (spelled in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">Canadian English</a>) opened in November 2006 in <a href="/wiki/Ancaster,_Ontario" title="Ancaster, Ontario">Ancaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stouffville,_Ontario" title="Stouffville, Ontario">Stouffville</a>, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The 100th<span class="nowrap"> </span>Canadian Supercentre opened in July 2010, in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a>.
</p><p>In 2010, approximately one year after its incorporation of Schedule 2 (foreign-owned, deposit-taking) of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Bank_Act_(Canada)" title="Bank Act (Canada)">Bank Act</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Walmart Canada Bank was introduced with the launch of the Walmart (Canada) Rewards MasterCard.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart_canada_bank_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart_canada_bank-162">[162]</a></sup> Less than ten years later, however, on May 17, 2018, <b>Wal-Mart Canada</b> announced it had reached a definitive agreement to sell Wal-Mart Canada Bank to <a href="/wiki/First_National_Financial_Corporation" title="First National Financial Corporation">First National</a> co-founder Stephen Smith and private equity firm <a href="/wiki/Centerbridge_Partners" title="Centerbridge Partners">Centerbridge Partners, L.P.</a>, on undisclosed financial terms, though it added that it would still be issuer of the Walmart (Canada) Rewards MasterCard.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>On the purely coincidental date of April 1, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Centerbridge_Partners" title="Centerbridge Partners">Centerbridge Partners, L.P.</a> and Stephen Smith jointly announced the closing of the previously announced acquisition of Wal-Mart Canada Bank and that it was to be renamed Duo Bank of Canada, to be styled simply as Duo Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Though exact ownership percentages were never revealed in either company announcement, it has also since been revealed that Duo Bank was reclassified as a Schedule 1 (domestic, deposit-taking)<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-osfi-wwr_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osfi-wwr-167">[167]</a></sup> federally chartered bank of the <i><a href="/wiki/Bank_Act_(Canada)" title="Bank Act (Canada)">Bank Act</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> from the Schedule 2 (foreign-owned or -controlled, deposit-taking)<sup id="cite_ref-osfi-wwr_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osfi-wwr-167">[167]</a></sup> that it had been, which indicates that Stephen Smith, as a noted Canadian businessman, is in a <a href="/wiki/Controlling_interest" title="Controlling interest">controlling</a> position.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: United Kingdom" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg/220px-A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="543"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 187px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg/220px-A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="187" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_big_green_sign_-_geograph.org.uk_-_781233.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a> store in March 2008</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart's UK subsidiary Asda (which retained its name after being acquired by Walmart) is based in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and accounted for 42.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent of 2006 sales of Walmart's international division. In contrast to the U.S. operations, Asda was originally and still remains primarily a grocery chain, but with a stronger focus on non-food items than most UK supermarket chains other than <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>. As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Asda had 631 stores,<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> including 147 from the 2010 acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Netto_UK" title="Netto UK">Netto UK</a>. In addition to small suburban Asda Supermarkets at 207 locations,<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> larger stores are branded Supercentres; there are 32 of these.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Other banners include Asda Superstores (341 locations), Asda Living (33 locations), and Asda Petrol Fueling Station (18 locations).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> In July 2015, Asda updated its logo featuring the Walmart Asterisks behind the first 'A' in the Logo. In May 2018, Walmart announced plans to sell Asda to rival <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury's">Sainsbury's</a> for $10.1 billion. Under the terms of the deal, Walmart would have received a 42% stake in the combined company and about £3 billion in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> However, in April 2019, the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Competition_and_Markets_Authority" title="Competition and Markets Authority">Competition and Markets Authority</a> blocked the proposed sale of Asda to Sainsburys.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Africa" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On September 28, 2010, Walmart announced it would buy <a href="/wiki/Massmart_Holdings_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Massmart Holdings Ltd">Massmart Holdings Ltd</a>. of <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> in a deal worth over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion</span> giving the company its first footprint in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Wake_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wake-171">[171]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> it has 442 stores, including 393 stores in South Africa (under the banners Game Foodco [79 locations], CBW [43 locations], Game [43 locations], Builders Express [49 locations], Builders Warehouse [33 locations], Cambridge [44 locations], Dion Wired [21 locations], Rhino [18 locations], Makro [22 locations], Builders Trade Depot [9 locations], Jumbo [13 locations], and Builders Superstore [19 locations]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 11 stores in Botswana (under the banners CBW [7 locations], Game Foodco [2 locations], and Builders Warehouse [2 locations]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 4 stores in Ghana (under the Game Foodco banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 3 stores in Kenya (under the Game Foodco banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 3 stores in Lesotho (under the banners CBW [2 locations] and Game Foodco [1 location]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup> 2 stores in Malawi (under the Game banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 6 stores in Mozambique (under the banners Builders Warehouse [2 locations], Game Foodco [2 locations], CBW [1 location], and Builders Express [1 location]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 5 stores in Namibia (under the banners Game Foodco [4 locations] and Game [1 location]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 5 stores in Nigeria (under the banners Game [3 locations] and Game Foodco [2 location]),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1 store in Swaziland (under the CBW banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1 store in Tanzania (under the Game banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> 1 store in Uganda (under the Game banner),<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> and 7 stores in Zambia (under the banners CBW [1 location], Game [3 locations], Builders Warehouse [2 locations], and Builders Express [1 location]).<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p><p><span id="Asia"></span>
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: China" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="An aisle in a Walmart store in China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg/170px-20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="4020"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 230px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg/170px-20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" data-alt="An aisle in a Walmart store in China" data-width="170" data-height="230" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20170212_Bilingual_signs_in_Walmart_Hangzhou_Toys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Walmart in <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, China in February 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart has joint ventures in China and several majority-owned subsidiaries. As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart China (沃尔玛 <i>Wò'ērmǎ</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> operates 438 stores under the Walmart Supercenter (404 locations), Sam's Club (26 locations) and Neighborhood Market (8 locations) banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2012, Walmart announced that the company raised its stake to 51 percent in Chinese online supermarket <a href="/wiki/Yihaodian" title="Yihaodian">Yihaodian</a> to tap rising consumer wealth and help the company offer more products. Walmart took full ownership in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Jourdan_15_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jourdan_15-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Japan" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In Japan, Walmart owns 100 percent of <a href="/wiki/Seiyu_Group" title="Seiyu Group">Seiyu</a> (西友 <i>Seiyū</i>) as of 2008.<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boyle_09_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyle_09-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020, there are 333 stores under the Seiyu (Hypermarket) (88 locations), Seiyu (Supermarket) (174 locations), Seiyu (General Merchandise) (1<span class="nowrap"> </span>location), Livin (6<span class="nowrap"> </span>locations), and Sunny (64<span class="nowrap"> </span>locations) banners.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: India" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In November 2006, the company announced a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Enterprises" title="Bharti Enterprises">Bharti Enterprises</a> to operate in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. As foreign corporations were not allowed to enter the retail sector directly, Walmart operated through franchises and handled the wholesale end of the business.<sup id="cite_ref-walmartindia_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmartindia-176">[176]</a></sup> The partnership involved two joint ventures—Bharti manages the front end, involving opening of retail outlets while Walmart takes care of the back end, such as <a href="/wiki/Cold_chain" title="Cold chain">cold chains</a> and logistics. Walmart operates stores in India under the name Best Price Modern Wholesale.<sup id="cite_ref-Mathew_13_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mathew_13-177">[177]</a></sup> The first store opened in <a href="/wiki/Amritsar" title="Amritsar">Amritsar</a> on May 30, 2009. On September 14, 2012, the Government of India approved 51 percent FDI in multi-brand retails, subject to approval by individual states, effective September 20, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Scott Price, Walmart's president and CEO for Asia, told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> that the company would be able to start opening Walmart stores in India within two years.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Expansion into India faced some significant problems. In November 2012, Walmart admitted to spending <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span> lobbying the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-indiatimes_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indiatimes-181">[181]</a></sup> lobbying is conventionally considered bribery in India.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCnewsUS_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCnewsUS-182">[182]</a></sup> Walmart is conducting an internal investigation into potential violations of the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Corrupt_Practices_Act" title="Foreign Corrupt Practices Act">Foreign Corrupt Practices Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTinquiry_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTinquiry-183">[183]</a></sup> Bharti Walmart suspended a number of employees, rumored to include its CFO and legal team, to ensure "a complete and thorough investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-NYTIndianBribery_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIndianBribery-184">[184]</a></sup> As of January 31, 2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are 28 Best Price locations.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> In October 2013, Bharti and Walmart separated to pursue business independently.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_of_India_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_of_India-185">[185]</a></sup></p><p>On May 9, 2018, Walmart announced its intent to acquire a 77% majority stake in the Indian e-commerce company <a href="/wiki/Flipkart" title="Flipkart">Flipkart</a> for $16 billion, in a deal that was completed on August 18, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Setbacks">Setbacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Setbacks" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In the mid-1990s, Walmart tried with a large financial investment to get a foothold in the German retail market. In 1997, Walmart took over the supermarket chain Wertkauf with its 21 stores for <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">DM</a> 750 million<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> and the following year Walmart acquired 74 Interspar stores for DM 1.3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> The German market at this point was an oligopoly with high competition among companies which used a similar low price strategy as Walmart. As a result, Walmart's low price strategy yielded no competitive advantage. Walmart's <a href="/wiki/Organizational_culture" title="Organizational culture">corporate culture</a> was not viewed positively among employees and customers, particularly Walmart's "statement of ethics", which attempted to restrict relationships between employees, a possible violation of German labor law, and led to a public discussion in the media, resulting in a bad reputation among customers.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In July 2006, Walmart announced its withdrawal from Germany due to sustained losses. The stores were sold to the German company <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Metro</a> during Walmart's fiscal third quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyle_09_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyle_09-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-walmartgermany_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmartgermany-194">[194]</a></sup> Walmart did not disclose its losses from its German investment, but they were estimated to be around €3 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG/220px-Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="278"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 96px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG/220px-Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="96" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hiper_Bompre%C3%A7o.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bompre%C3%A7o" title="Bompreço">Hiper Bompreço</a> in <a href="/wiki/Natal,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Natal, Brazil">Natal, Brazil</a> in May 2008</div></div></div>
<p>In 2004, Walmart bought the 118<span class="nowrap"> </span>stores in the <a href="/wiki/Bompre%C3%A7o" title="Bompreço">Bompreço</a> supermarket chain in northeastern Brazil. In late 2005, it took control of the Brazilian operations of <a href="/wiki/Sonae" title="Sonae">Sonae</a> Distribution Group through its new subsidiary, WMS Supermercados do Brasil, thus acquiring control of the Nacional and Mercadorama supermarket chains, the leaders in the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">Rio Grande do Sul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paraná (state)">Paraná</a> states, respectively. None of these stores were rebranded. As of January 2014,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart operated 61 Bompreço supermarkets, 39<span class="nowrap"> </span>Hiper Bompreço stores. It also ran 57<span class="nowrap"> </span>Walmart Supercenters, 27<span class="nowrap"> </span>Sam's Clubs, and 174 Todo Dia stores. With the acquisition of Bompreço and Sonae, by 2010, Walmart was the third-largest supermarket chain in Brazil, behind <a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> and <a href="/wiki/GPA_(company)" title="GPA (company)">Pão de Açúcar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WalmartBrazil_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WalmartBrazil-196">[196]</a></sup></p><p>Walmart Brasil, the operating company, has its head office in <a href="/wiki/Barueri" title="Barueri">Barueri</a>, São Paulo State, and regional offices in <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, Paraná; <a href="/wiki/Porto_Alegre" title="Porto Alegre">Porto Alegre</a>, Rio Grande do Sul; <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">Recife</a>, Pernambuco; and <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, Bahia.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Walmart Brasil operates under the banners Todo Dia, Nacional, Bompreço, Walmart Supercenter, Maxxi Atacado, Hipermercado Big, Hiper Bompreço, Sam's Club, Mercadorama, Walmart Posto (Gas Station), Supermercado Todo Dia, and Hiper Todo Dia.<sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage_1-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_&amp;_Square_Footage-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unit_Counts_by_Country_2-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unit_Counts_by_Country-2">[2]</a></sup> Recently, the company started the conversion process of all Hiper Bompreço and Big stores into Walmart Supercenters and Bompreço, Nacional and Mercadorama stores into the Walmart Supermercado brand.
</p><p>Since August 2018, Walmart Inc. only holds a minority stake in Walmart Brasil, which was renamed Grupo Big on August 12, 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> with 20% of the company's shares, and <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> firm <a href="/wiki/Advent_International" title="Advent International">Advent International</a> holding 80% ownership of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-AdventWalmartBrazil_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdventWalmartBrazil-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_charges">Corruption charges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Corruption charges" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>An April 2012 investigation by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported the allegations of a former executive of Walmart de Mexico that, in September 2005, the company had paid <a href="/wiki/Bribery" title="Bribery">bribes</a> via local fixers to officials throughout Mexico in exchange for construction permits, information, and other favors, which gave Walmart a substantial advantage over competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTBribe_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTBribe-200">[200]</a></sup> Walmart investigators found credible evidence that Mexican and American laws had been broken. Concerns were also raised that Walmart executives in the United States had "hushed up" the allegations. A follow-up investigation by <i>The New York Times</i>, published December 17, 2012, revealed evidence that regulatory permission for siting, construction, and operation of nineteen stores had been obtained through bribery. There was evidence that a bribe of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$52,000</span> was paid to change a zoning map, which enabled the opening of a Walmart store a mile from a historical site in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Teotihuacán">San Juan Teotihuacán</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT92904_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT92904-201">[201]</a></sup> After the initial article was released, Walmart released a statement denying the allegations and describing its anti-corruption policy. While an official Walmart report states that it had found no evidence of corruption, the article alleges that previous internal reports had indeed turned up such evidence before the story became public.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine contributor Adam Hartung also commented that the bribery scandal was a reflection of Walmart's "serious management and strategy troubles", stating, "[s]candals are now commonplace<span class="nowrap"> </span>... [e]ach scandal points out that Walmart's strategy is harder to navigate and is running into big problems".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, there was an incident with CJ's Seafood, a crawfish processing firm in Louisiana that was partnered with Walmart, that eventually gained media attention for the mistreatment of its 40 H-2B visa workers from Mexico. These workers experienced harsh living conditions in tightly packed trailers outside of the work facility, physical threats, verbal abuse and were forced to work day-long shifts. Many of the workers were afraid to take action about the abuse due to the fact that the manager threatened the lives of their family members in the U.S. and Mexico if the abuse were to be reported. Eight of the workers confronted management at CJ's Seafood about the mistreatment; however, the management denied the abuse allegations and the workers went on strike. The workers then took their stories to Walmart due to their partnership with CJ's. While Walmart was investigating the situation, the workers collected 150,000 signatures of supporters who agreed that Walmart should stand by the workers and take action. In June 2012, the visa workers held a protest and day-long hunger strike outside of the apartment building where a Walmart board member resided. Following this protest, Walmart announced its final decision to no longer work with CJ's Seafood. Less than a month later, the Department of Labor fined CJ's Seafood "approximately $460,000 in back-pay, safety violations, wage and hour violations, civil damages and fines for abuses to the H-2B program. The company has since shut down."<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p><p>As of December 2012,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> internal investigations were ongoing into possible violations of the Foreign Corrupt Practices Act.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT121712_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT121712-205">[205]</a></sup> Walmart has invested <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$99<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span> on internal investigations, which expanded beyond Mexico to implicate operations in China, Brazil, and India.<sup id="cite_ref-Clifford_12_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clifford_12-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_12_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_12-207">[207]</a></sup> The case has added fuel to the debate as to whether foreign investment will result in increased prosperity, or if it merely allows local retail trade and economic policy to be taken over by "foreign financial and corporate interests".<sup id="cite_ref-Sharma_12_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma_12-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTIndia_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIndia-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Sam.27s_Club"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sam's_Club">Sam's Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sam's Club" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg/220px-Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2364" data-file-height="2000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 186px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg/220px-Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="186" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sam%27s_Club_store.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Sam's Club store in <a href="/wiki/Maplewood,_Missouri" title="Maplewood, Missouri">Maplewood, Missouri</a> in April 2006</div></div></div>
<p><b>Sam's Club</b> is a chain of <a href="/wiki/Warehouse_club" title="Warehouse club">warehouse clubs</a> that sell groceries and <a href="/wiki/General_merchandise" class="mw-redirect" title="General merchandise">general merchandise</a>, often in bulk. Locations generally range in size from 32,000–168,000 sq ft (3,000–15,600 m<sup>2</sup>), with an average club size of approximately 134,000 sq ft (12,400 m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-2020_10-K_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020_10-K-11">[11]</a></sup> The first Sam's Club was opened by Walmart, Inc. in 1983 in <a href="/wiki/Midwest_City,_Oklahoma" title="Midwest City, Oklahoma">Midwest City, Oklahoma</a><sup id="cite_ref-aboutsamsclub_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutsamsclub-210">[210]</a></sup> under the name "Sam's Wholesale Club". The chain was named after its founder Sam Walton. As of January, 2019, Sam's Club operated 599 membership warehouse clubs and accounted for 11.3% of Walmart's revenue at $57.839 billion in fiscal year 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-xbrlus_1_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xbrlus_1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> Kathryn McLay is the president and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart.com_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart.com-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_eCommerce">Global eCommerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Global eCommerce" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Based in San Bruno, California, Walmart's Global eCommerce division provides online retailing for Walmart, Sam's Club, Asda, and all other international brands. There are several locations in the United States in California and Oregon: <a href="/wiki/San_Bruno,_California" title="San Bruno, California">San Bruno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California" title="Sunnyvale, California">Sunnyvale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane,_California" title="Brisbane, California">Brisbane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a>. Locations outside of the United States include <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> (<a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a> (India). Marc Lore is the president and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-walmart.com_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walmart.com-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Subsidiaries" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Vudu">Vudu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Vudu" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vudu_2014_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="Blue vudu logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/220px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="61" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="83"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 61px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/220px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png" data-alt="Blue vudu logo" data-width="220" data-height="61" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/330px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Vudu_2014_logo.svg/440px-Vudu_2014_logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vudu_2014_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vudu logo</div></div></div>
<p>In February 2010, Walmart agreed to buy <a href="/wiki/Vudu" title="Vudu">Vudu</a>, a Silicon Valley start-up whose online movie service is being built into an increasing number of televisions and Blu-ray players. Terms of the acquisition were not disclosed, but a person briefed on the deal said the price for the company, which raised <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$60<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span> in capital, was over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100<span class="nowrap"> </span>million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stone_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone-213">[213]</a></sup> Vudu is the third-most-popular online movie service, with a market share of 5.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_label_brands">Private label brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Private label brands" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Walmart_brands" title="List of Walmart brands">List of Walmart brands</a></div>
<p>About 40 percent of products sold in Walmart are <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a> <a href="/wiki/Store_brand" class="mw-redirect" title="Store brand">store brands</a>, which are produced for the company through contracts with manufacturers. Walmart began offering private label brands in 1991, with the launch of <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Choice" title="Sam's Choice">Sam's Choice</a>, a line of drinks produced by <a href="/wiki/Cott" title="Cott">Cott</a> Beverages for Walmart. Sam's Choice quickly became popular and by 1993, was the third-most-popular beverage brand in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-samschoice_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samschoice-215">[215]</a></sup> Other Walmart brands include Great Value and Equate in the U.S. and Canada and Smart Price in Britain. A 2006 study talked of "the magnitude of mind-share Walmart appears to hold in the shoppers' minds when it comes to the awareness of private label brands and retailers."<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Entertainment" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, the company teamed with <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> to produce <i><a href="/wiki/Secrets_of_the_Mountain" title="Secrets of the Mountain">Secrets of the Mountain</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jensen_Project" title="The Jensen Project">The Jensen Project</a></i>, two-hour family movies which featured the characters using Walmart and Procter &amp; Gamble-branded products. <i>The Jensen Project</i> also featured a preview of a product to be released in several months in Walmart stores.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-la_times_review_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-la_times_review-218">[218]</a></sup> A third movie, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Walk_in_My_Shoes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="A Walk in My Shoes (page does not exist)">A Walk in My Shoes</a></i>, also aired in 2010 and a fourth is in production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Walmart's director of brand marketing also serves as co-chair of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_National_Advertisers" title="Association of National Advertisers">Association of National Advertisers</a>'s Alliance for Family Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_commerce_acquisitions_and_plans">Online commerce acquisitions and plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Online commerce acquisitions and plans" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In September 2016, Walmart purchased <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> company <a href="/wiki/Jet.com" title="Jet.com">Jet.com</a>, founded in 2014 by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Lore" title="Marc Lore">Marc Lore</a>, to start competing with Amazon.com. Jet.com has acquired its own share of online retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Hayneedle" title="Hayneedle">Hayneedle</a> in March 2016, Shoebuy.com in December 2016, and <a href="/wiki/ModCloth" title="ModCloth">ModCloth</a> in March 2017. Walmart also acquired Parcel, a delivery service in New York, on September 29, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT9162018_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT9162018-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walmart91718_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart91718-222">[222]</a></sup></p><p>On February 15, 2017, Walmart acquired <a href="/wiki/Moosejaw" title="Moosejaw">Moosejaw</a>, an online active outdoor retailer, for approximately $51 million. Moosejaw brought with it partnerships with more than 400 brands, including <a href="/wiki/Patagonia_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Patagonia (clothing)">Patagonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_North_Face" title="The North Face">The North Face</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marmot_(company)" title="Marmot (company)">Marmot</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arc%27teryx" title="Arc'teryx">Arc'teryx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Marc_Lore" title="Marc Lore">Marc Lore</a>, Walmart's U.S. e-commerce CEO, said that Walmart's existing physical infrastructure of almost 5,000 stores around the U.S. will enhance their digital expansion by doubling as warehouses for e-commerce without increasing overhead.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> As of 2017,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Walmart offers in-store pickup for online orders at 1,000 stores with plans to eventually expand the service to all of its stores.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p><p>On May 9, 2018, Walmart announced its intent to acquire a 77% controlling stake in the Indian e-commerce website <a href="/wiki/Flipkart" title="Flipkart">Flipkart</a> for $16 billion<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> (beating bids by Amazon.com), subject to regulatory approval. Following its completion, the website's management will report to Marc Lore.<sup id="cite_ref-Walmart-Inc-May-2018-8-K_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walmart-Inc-May-2018-8-K-227">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Completion of the deal was announced on August 18, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup></p><p>The company's partnership with subscription service <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kidbox&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kidbox (page does not exist)">Kidbox</a> was announced on April 16, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Walmart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg/220px-Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2100"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 308px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg/220px-Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="308" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Walmart_Home_Office_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Home office in <a href="/wiki/Bentonville,_Arkansas" title="Bentonville, Arkansas">Bentonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a> in June 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Walmart is headquartered in the Walmart Home Office complex in Bentonville, Arkansas. The company's <a href="/wiki/Business_model" title="Business model">business model</a> is based on selling a wide variety of general merchandise at low prices.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Annual_Report_Page_19-9">[9]</a></sup> Doug McMillon became Walmart's CEO on February 1, 2014. He has also worked as the head of Sam's Club and Walmart International.<sup id="cite_ref-O'Keefe_15_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O'Keefe_15-232">[232]</a></sup> The company refers to its employees as "associates". All Walmart stores in the U.S. and Canada also have designated "<a href="/wiki/Walmart_greeter" title="Walmart greeter">greeters</a>" at the entrance, a practice pioneered by Sam Walton and later imitated by other retailers. Greeters are trained to help shoppers find what they want and answer their questions.<sup id="cite_ref-Kendall_Gerald_I_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kendall_Gerald_I-233">[233]</a></sup></p><p>For many years, associates were identified in the store by their signature blue vest, but this practice was discontinued in June 2007 and replaced with khaki pants and polo shirts. The wardrobe change was part of a larger corporate overhaul to increase sales and rejuvenate the company's stock price.<sup id="cite_ref-replace_blue_vests_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-replace_blue_vests-234">[234]</a></sup> In September 2014, the uniform was again updated to bring back a vest (paid for by the company) for store employees over the same polos and khaki or black pants paid for by the employee. The vest is navy blue for Walmart employees at Supercenters and discount stores, lime green for Walmart Neighborhood Market employees and yellow for self check out associates; door greeters and customer service managers. Both state "Proud Walmart Associate" on the left breast and the "Spark" logo covering the back.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Reportedly one of the main reasons the vest was reintroduced was that some customers had trouble identifying employees.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> In 2016, self-checkout associates, door greeters and customer service managers began wearing a yellow vest to be better seen by customers. By requiring employees to wear uniforms that are made up of standard "street wear", Walmart is not required to purchase or reimbursement employees which is required in some states, as long as that clothing can be worn elsewhere. Businesses are only legally required to pay for branded shirts and pants or clothes that would be difficult to wear outside of work.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p><p>Unlike many other retailers, Walmart does not charge <a href="/wiki/Slotting_fee" title="Slotting fee">slotting fees</a> to suppliers for their products to appear in the store.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson-238">[238]</a></sup> Instead, it focuses on selling more-popular products and provides incentives for store managers to drop unpopular products.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson-238">[238]</a></sup></p><p>From 2006 to 2010, the company eliminated its <a href="/wiki/Layaway" title="Layaway">layaway</a> program. In 2011, the company revived its layaway program.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></p><p>Walmart introduced its Site-To-Store program in 2007, after testing the program since 2004 on a limited basis.
